<user_name>Joe Freeman (Joe)</user_name><time>1439717103635< /time><rating>5</rating>< text>
This place is just like the two Greek Chicken branches in nearby El Cajon, only a lot less crowded. The food is always fresh and delicious and the place is spotless. We usually get the single-skewer chicken kabob dinner, which consists of five or six large chunks of grilled chicken breast on a skewer, a big side of Greek-style rice, four quarters of pita bread, and a substantial and delicious Greek salad packed into a small bowl. You order at the counter and they call your number when your order is ready, so there's really no service and it's probably fine not to leave a tip, making the total cost for my usual meal only about twelve bucks without a drink. We go here several times a month and it never disappoints.</text>

Very clean.  Immaculately stocked shelves. Great selection of basic Asian cooking staples.  A nice surprise find.

Found this place by accident while stopping by to grab food at Harry's Cafe.  Decided to take a peak inside after noticing they had a sign for BBQ pork and other take-out food.  Was very pleased to find some very nice fresh veggies. They didn't have a huge selection,  but did have my favorites, bok choy, gai lan and long green beans.  The shelves are packed with Asian sundries and very well organized and everything was very clean.  The owners obviously take a lot of pride maintaining their store.</text>

All kinds of specialty Asian cuisine items such as dried mushrooms, various teas and spices, pickled quail eggs, Taiwan Style Herbal Gelatin, etc. Somewhat unusual produce like kohlrabi and bitter melon. Mid-November and they had Napa Cabbage for 99 cents. They also sell cooked-to-order chow mein, fried rice, and other dishes for $6 per pound or so. Peking Spare Ribs, Empress Chicken, and duck for a little more. Be aware, though, that they only accept cash.< /review>

113939810180248887620<//UserId.>
< name>
Miriam Robarts<//name>
<Time>1469255865272</Time><rate>4</rate>< text>
Wing Fa Market is a tiny Chinese market packed with asian groceries and some fresh produce. They also have roasted meats, take out, and bakery items.

I went by yesterday to see if they had Gai Mei Bao (Chinese Coconut Cocktail Buns). The clerk I spoke to had a strong accent, but she was very friendly and quickly grabbed a scrap of paper to write on to help me understand her. I appreciated her help and I didn't feel out out place as a white girl in a Chinese store. She said they would have some the next day and asked if I wanted some Pork buns, as she took down an order for me. When I came in today, she recognized me and I didn't even have to mention my order! The other customers were friendly as well.

I have tried a couple of other places in Sacramento for Gai Mei Bao, and I think this one is the best. I also enjoyed their Pork Bao. Yum! I think they only get the bakery items on Friday afternoons (around 12:30). A long line quickly formed as I waited for the delivery to arrive, so you might want to place an order ahead of time.

So, not only were the Bao delicious, but a very good price! The Pork buns were $0.90 each and the Gai Mei Bao were $0.45 each! Awesome! (But they don't take credit cards!)

They have take-out, but it looked like there were only six items (some available as chicken or pork), and one very large size. Next time, I will come early before the rush and ask them more about their take-out dishes. I got a box of fried rice, for about $6.00. You get a lot for the price, and they went in back to cook it--so you have to wait--but it's fresh. I perused the grocery isles and picked up some Hoisin sauce while I waited. The fried rice was ok, but I didn't think it had a lot of flavor. (Maybe because I really wanted the Chow Mein, but had to avoid it due to a temporary diet restriction.) I added some soy sauce and my newly-purchased hoisin sauce to my fried rice when I got home, and enjoyed it more that way.

Directions:
It's a little hard to spot, since it's a very small store, and there are trees in front. If you're coming down 16th Street, from HWY 50, it's just past U St. on the left (after Kiyo's Floral Design, Harry's Cafe, and an empty looking building). There is a sign on the side of the building, which you can see from this direction, if you're looking for it.< /text>

<Review>They have a $59.95 promotion where you can get 2 glasses and an eye exam. It's a pretty good deal but watch out for the limited stock of these promotional glasses and the upsales!  There are only a  limited amount of these promotional glasses, like 20 pairs per section (men's, women's, etc). All the other glasses are priced higher and you get to pay for the more expensive of the 2 that you decide to get.  Then, if you want thinner lenses, bifocals, progressive, tinting or any extra niceties, it'll cost you more, sometimes a lot more. In addition, there were only 3 employees there and they were always juggling customers.

The day I went in, there wasn't an optometrist on the premises (Only on Mondays, apparently) so my eye exam was conducted remotely by a person on a computer monitor. She did a good job and produced a prescription for me. However, it was just for glasses and they needed to contact the doctor to get an updated prescription for contacts. That took an hour so I asked them what the holdup was and they said that they have to get an approval from the remote doctor but they didn't send the contact prescription so the technician has me redo the test again.  All in all, I was in there from 10:15 AM until 1:30 PM. That was way too long! I ended up getting another complete eye exam which they didn't charge me for but that ultimately was good because they got the response from the doctor quickly and I was able to pay my bill and get out eventually.< /Review>< pictures>

<rate>3< /rate><Review>UPDATED REVIEW 12/11/2018 - - -
Okaaay, I came back because of a Groupon that caught my attention. It was $150 for $32. I thought, "hey, now I can get a third awesome pair of glasses!"-- I knew I was going to be paying a little more than expected but.. dang, I almost regretted getting the Groupon at all. Quite the different experience than when I visited and reviewed back in April..

Upon arriving, they had no idea I was coming although I had called ahead and made an appointment. I initially spoke to Ivan who didn't know my name or why I was there. Quite the bummer since I explained everything over the phone. He informed me that I had called 'support line' instead of the actual store. Nevertheless, he was very willing to help me.

As much as he could, at least..

I explained to him I wanted the exact same type of glasses I had ordered back in April and was hoping to get them for the L O W L O W since I had the $150 Groupon. That's when he informed me he would try to "help me out" because he wouldn't be able to use that coupon with the pricing I received before. Maaaaaan.. I didn't get upset but it did make me roll my eyes and it let me know I had walked into a "used car dealership" kind of vibe. Huge bummer and very 'scam-esque'..

As much as Ivan wanted to help, there was still a tug-of-war between him and I. Where he wanted to try to get every single penny he could out of me and I wanted to save every single penny I could. I mean, I walked in there with a Groupon after all~.. I'm clearly trying to save some cash, man!

I wasn't rolling over for him and he (said he) couldn't provide me with the price I was looking for. I had walked in there thinking, "I'll pay $30 for my frames via Amazon, $32 for the Groupon and pay another.. what?.. $30 bucks at Stanton? Heck, let's make it $40 bucks! I'll get another pair for a total of ~$100 for a new pair altogether." -- that was not the case AT ALL. Ivan tried to get me to pay something like.. $170 for BETTER glasses (Ivan, if you're reading this, sorry if I forgot the exact amount, but it was ridiculous, man!). I cleaaarly wasn't having that. He then said something like $130? and that was totally not flying for me.

We WERE NOT on the same page..
Ivan had clearly had enough. I had communicated with him that it really felt like he was on commission and didn't want to go through all struggle. I wanted (again) the L O W L O W . I didn't want him asking him, "what's the most you want to spend today?". Like.. come on, man. Want me to say ten bucks? After some miscommunication, Ivan was visibly frustrated (and I get it.. I was NOT about to pay $100 bucks and he wasn't budging).

He said the magic word: Manager.

Nick came in to save the day.
He was much more understanding and had more power to get me a much more reasonable price. He got me the same pair of glasses I got earlier this year for $55 dollars. I was happy with that. Win some, Lose some.

Unfortunately, after this experience, I wouldn't recommend this store to EVERYONE. If you do decide you're brave enough, make sure you're ready to bargain and fight a little bit, like at the swap meet. Or if you have sales experience, that helps too!

I don't wanna give Nick anything lower than 3 stars after he hooked me up.

<Date>1464713436026<//Date><Rating>4<//Rating>< review>
usually as you get closer to the beach, the food get shittier and you end up paying up for location and scene. and venice to me is pretty mediocre overall as far as food. but leona is actually decent in terms of food, and i'd probably come here again for the food.

had the bulgogi short ribs. well, it's not really bulgogi in terms of flavor. i really don't know why they call it that. but it was good, and the short rib was braised and cooked nicely...very tender as you would expect. comes with bone marrow on the side, but that's not my thing.

had a bit of the risotto. less impressed with that, but it was okay, as well. a friend had the chicken which looked like a square. not sure what was up with that, but he said it tasted good.

one bummer is the parking situation. $9 for valet.< /review>

<Text>My time spent inside "Crust" was less than 5 minutes. I simply picked up a pizza to go.  I inhaled the environment of "Crust" in those few minutes.

The 5 stars I gave was 95 percent for the pizza and 5 percent for my short experience inside and over the phone ordering.

If your a serious pizza lover that appreciates quality and taste, this place is top tier for you.  Traveling often for business I get around the US and can tell you "Crust" is in the top 10 percent. (Been to NY and Chicago, interesting enough, and never had time to get pizza)

I created my own pizza.
I had a 10" pizza with Artisan crust (regular), Wisconsin mozzarella cheese, Portobello mushrooms, black olives and onions. My total was 14.85 and that was for two people. No complaints, your getting quality.  First and final opinion is this place has great pizza.  The only local pizza equal is "Marco's" in Vista, CA.

I will come here again, and I live in San Marcos 6 miles away.

The environment inside made me think i was inside"Chipotle" with servers and a bar added. That is not saying a bad thing. I am just  describing the inside as best I can. Wide beer and wine selection.  I interacted with three employees and they were all friendly. Others will probably disagree, but I PERSONALLY would not go there with a group bigger than 6. Customer service over the phone for the order was great. Plenty of parking.

Pizzaholic tourists getting the "shakes" should definitely go here if in Carlsbad, CA.</Text><Pictures>None</Pictures>< response>

< text>
I just Stopped by there on Wednesday afternoon-ish when I drove back to South Bay from near Mexico and the place was cozy, peaceful, down to earth vibe, clean and  dry/steam sauna and Jacuzzi Were nice. I didn't use bio rooms, warm room etc...thus can't comment on that.
I was so tired from driving, stress from work etc ..requested 1 hour massage (their rate was so reasonable compare to other Spa /massage places) and Never regretted.
The massage guy was an Asian, he was nice, very professional & very easy on the eyes...his skill was phenomenal, satisfying and very soothing/relaxing session made me feel refreshed afterwards. If you expect some kinda happy ending/sexual services from the massage guy, keep looking elsewhere. All he does is just giving the superb massage & I'm totally fine with it. next time I go to the area, I'll stop by this place again just to get a massage from him.
Enjoyed this place much better than other Korean style Spas I visited before in whole LA area.< /text>

<time>1559680004660<//time><Rating>5</Rating>< review>
Just went in for an 3D scan as part of an approved free re-evaluation since I was unhappy with the straightening of my lower teeth after finishing my course of initial aligners.
I originally made my molds at home with a kit I bought at CVS because didn't want to drive to Hollywood for a scan (the nearest SmileShop at the time).
Raul was friendly, utterly professional and really took the time to make sure my second round of aligners were going to get me the results I want.
After the scan which took less than 5 minutes, Raul sat with me and we went tooth by tooth in the area of my concern to determine exactly what needed to happen to each tooth to achieve my ideal straightened smile. Then he made sure I had answers to all my questions about timing, retainer use, etc.
After my experience with Raul at the Beverly Hills SmileShop I wish I had done the 3D scan from the beginning. Logistically it takes a fourth of the time than doing your own molds at home packing and shipping them - total time in and out 20 minutes - can't beat that! Moreover, it felt like the dental professional assigned to my case is going to have better impressions of my teeth and more complete information, with the help of Raul, to ensure my next round of aligners are going to get me to my ideal smile.</review>

< Review>
So far got the 3D scan done today. Wish I had someone more knowledgable with this process as the person helping me is just a tech that works with the 3D scanner. I think I had a trainee which is okay, but it felt like someone shoving a massive toothbrush pretending to brush my teeth very nervously with no bedside manner. I just hope the scan came out good for the approved offsite dentist/orthodontists to be able to properly see all my teeth to determine how long the process of straightening my teeth would be.

They had a salesperson approach with the typical building rapport and learning the word tracks of what to say when asked a question. I didn't have a lot of questions but the response of not asking too many questions as "most people have" was a bit alarming so I wanted to do more research after my visit. Look at all the youtube videos and reviews before you do this.

This apparently will not solve your under bite or over bite. As a matter of fact, if you have crowded lower teeth and spaced out upper teeth, and currently your teeth are aligned... You will develop an underbite as they close out your upper gaps and space out your lower teeth...

This makes me afraid. I wish they had mentioned this before I handed over my payment information.

I still got a deal on what the procedure will be. I've always have been self conscious of my smile. The debate really is if this will cause the wear on my teeth for having the smile I want. Once your teeth are straightened, your bite will be different. Everyone that has reviewed have mentioned, their bite isn't 100%.

Proceeding with caution for now...

Be sure to ask a ton of questions. üò¨</Review>
